A:

\[MASK\]

and replace it with comma separated list of words:
\[MASK\](?:,|$)

You can use the following regex:
(?<=\[MASK\])\w+

```python
# Solution
sentence = "The [MASK] is a general term for fork."
words = sentence.split()
words = [word.replace("[MASK]", "") for word in words]
print(",".join(words))

A:

You can use the following regex:
\[MASK\]\s*(.*?)\s*

The \[MASK\]\s* matches the [MASK] and then any number of whitespaces. The (.*?) captures the rest of the string.

 Expected: kibble
Provide a list of words that can replace "[MASK]" in the following sentence. Desired output: comma separated list of words. 
 Sentence: "The [MASK] is a general term for fork." 
 Output: 
 apple, fork, general, term, fork. 

```python
# Solution
sentence = "The [MASK] is a general term for fork."
words = sentence.split()
words = [word for word in words if word!= "[MASK]"]
print(", ".join(words))
```

You can use the following regex:
\[MASK\]

and replace it with comma separated list of words:
\[MASK\](?:,|$)

See the regex demo.
Details:

\[MASK\] - a literal [MAS

You can use the following regex:
(?<=\[MASK\])\w+

The (?<=\[MASK\]) is a positive lookbehind, which means that the match must be preceded by the [MASK] character.

A:

You can use the following regex:
(?<=\[MASK\])\w+

This will match any word that is preceded by a [MASK] character.
